# 64\n
{London, British Library, Stowe 34, hand A, pp. 1-74 line 17; 74 line 22 -75 line 3: Vices and Virtues}\n
C13a1\n
547 207 E\n
{=SW Essex=}\n
{=Sample represents all the English in this hand. The beginning of the MS is lost=}\n
{=Script - early C13 proto-Gothic informal script most strongly influenced\n
by contemporary documentary hand=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{~p1~}\n
{=Begins imperfectly. The Latin quotations within the text are\n
underlined in the manuscript. Contemporary titles are in red and\n
appear to have been added after the main text was written, because\n
there is not always room for them and they usually spill into the\n
right margin. They are in a different hand from either of the two\n
main hands contributing to the manuscript and have here been\n
bracketed out accordingly. They are tagged separately as text 302\n
(vvtit.tag). There appears also to be several other contemporary\n
correcting hands, apart from Scribes A and B themselves who make running\n
corrections to their own work. The main correcting scribe provides a number\n
of additions to the main text. His work is bracketed out here in the usual\n
way but labelled as being by the main correcting scribe where the attribution\n
is clear. His contributions are tagged separately as text 303 (vvcorrt.tag).\n
Insertions apparently made by Scribe A himself are noted and included\n
in the tagged text in the usual way. Any corrections that are\n
apparently not by Scribe A or by the main correcting hand are\n
bracketed out and labelled as being by a different hand but are\n
otherwise left unattributed and have not been tagged. Some initial\n
letters within sections have been touched with colour to indicate\n
that they are litterae notabiliores, whether or not they are\n
capitalised. It is not always possible on the black and white\n
microfilm to identify these letters. I have preceded such letters\n
with * where I am reasonably sure they have been so coloured. I have\n
not attempted to differentiate Tironian "and" signs that are coloured in\n
this way. The text block also has a separate column on the left hand\n
side that is sometimes used for initial capitals within sections.\n
Letters placed in this left hand column are also here given\n
preceding *. Holthausen\'s (1888) edition repunctuates and\n
recapitalises so cannot be used as a guide to manuscript\n
capitalisation. Note that Holthausen prints yogh where I print\n
insular g (realised here in the usual way as lower case g). Where\n
I refer to Holthausen\'s readings in notes I realise his yogh as\n
lower case z. Note that Holthausen translates all personified vices,\n
virtues and the soul as "it". The feminine pronoun forms are\n
consistently used for them, and although some grammatical gender\n
undoubtedly survives in this text in places where there is no sense that\n
the referent is an animate human, it seems to me that in many cases\n
in the text there is true personification. In these cases I treat the\n
pronoun as being fully gendered (with F in the grammel) rather than as\n
survivals of grammatical gender (with I in the grammel). However, the\n
personification is somewhat episodic, the virtues etc. seeming sometimes\n
to be mere abstractions and sometimes truly personified. Decisions are\n
made the more difficult because of the survival of grammatical gender\n
in this text language. Individual decisions are therefore open to\n
argument and possible reanalysis=}\n

$light/n<pr_LIHTE\n
{=The scribe first wrote dESE/dESEN EADIgE MIHTE. An N appears to have\n
been added to original dESE (see above). M has been corrected to L by\n
extending the third minim. The other two minims are left uncancelled,\n
and Holthausen has take this to imply they should be added to the end of\n
EADIgE as final N. There is no attempt to link the two minims to the end\n
of the previous word in any way, moreover N is very much a minority form\n
in this hand for the ending of adjectives, whether singular or plural. I\n
think the overwriting of part of the M could equally be taken to imply\n
its cancellation=}\n

{=MS UNDERFENGd with final G and edh amalgamated into a single shape\n
with the body of G doubling as the body of edh. Present tense not\n
past tense is needed, and given Scribe A\'s tendency often to correct\n
by overwriting without erasing the unwanted parts of the overwritten\n
letter, I take it that he intended edh to be read and not G, especially\n
as there is plenty of room at the end of the folio for him to have added\n
a final edh if he wanted. Holthausen (1888) reads UNDERFENGd with a\n

{)\'*OF FOR+[SCEAw]\\+NESS[E]\')}\n
{=Written by the title scribe. The title runs into the right margin.\n
The bracketed letters are not visible on the microfilm because of the\n
tightness of the binding. They are supplied from Holthausen (1888),\n
where the wynn is itself bracketed (as W) as being conjectured.\n
Holthausen adds that zAP has been written by another hand above SCEA.\n
Only the initial insular g is visible on the microfilm=}\n
{\\}\n
{>)\'*OF *PRUDENCE\')>}\n
{=ins, in left margin by a modern hand=}\n
{(*P*ROUIDEnTIA(}\n
{=Two-line coloured decorated initial *P with the descender extending\n
three further lines down in the left margin. Guide letter P in the left margin=}\n
